        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163005287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8391234803902427736">I have to say I was won over by the book. At first, it annoyed me -- I thought Kundera was trying to be clever. But then as I continued reading I realised the overall structure of the novel, and I realised he wasn't trying to be clever: he was sincerely trying to understand desire and love. Kundera is very intelligent and it shows -- there is a lot one could think about with regards to love and desire -- a lot of interesting ideas in the novel which he tries to understand. He is not really the m</span>
  <span id="freeText8391234803902427736" style="display:none">I have to say I was won over by the book. At first, it annoyed me -- I thought Kundera was trying to be clever. But then as I continued reading I realised the overall structure of the novel, and I realised he wasn't trying to be clever: he was sincerely trying to understand desire and love. Kundera is very intelligent and it shows -- there is a lot one could think about with regards to love and desire -- a lot of interesting ideas in the novel which he tries to understand. He is not really the most visionary writer but he certainly is very sensitive and intelligent. Kundera is just as lost as the reader is, where such emotions are concerned, and I find that admission of humility touching. The artists he discusses are spot on, at least where I'm concerned: if you want to talk about love -- Rilke, Goethe, Beethoven. Kundera writes with an intuitive understanding of great art and a critical mind, and it is a powerful combination. The book will take you where you want to go. But it will not tell you where you want to go, and in that sense some people might find it confusing and not so enjoyable. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8391234803902427736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15875260?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/54697-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=won-t-read-again">won-t-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=fictions-of-the-big-it">fictions-of-the-big-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54697-matt?shelf=worldly-lit">worldly-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15875260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7889591173766731542"><br/>Another clunker from Kundera- based on a captivating premise indeed and uniquely realized in parts but overall far too self-conscious, cerebral, gimmicky, and precious.<br/><br/>He spends an enormous amount of time describing this elliptical gesture one character makes and its epiphanic qualities for the rest of the narrative. I got it, quickly, I ain't too bright but I do dig the luminous renderings of everyday life quite a bit. O I was on board with that, but the rest of it was as much a hazy mush to me</span>
  <span id="freeText7889591173766731542" style="display:none"><br />Another clunker from Kundera- based on a captivating premise indeed and uniquely realized in parts but overall far too self-conscious, cerebral, gimmicky, and precious.<br /><br />He spends an enormous amount of time describing this elliptical gesture one character makes and its epiphanic qualities for the rest of the narrative. I got it, quickly, I ain't too bright but I do dig the luminous renderings of everyday life quite a bit. O I was on board with that, but the rest of it was as much a hazy mush to me when I read it as a recent-grad at 22 in lumberous hours on the couch in the living room as it is to me now, older wiser and as not about to shy away from abstraction's gauntlet as I ever was. <br /><br />Some people (many, even) wiser and brighter and more talented than myself swear by this guy but I just don't see it. O well, I hear The Joke is pretty good. Maybe someday...</span>

<div id="review_2570412323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570412323" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54104095-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569241095p2/54104095.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2570412323?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/54104095-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54104095-tom?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570412323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7449297209144917922">I genuinely don't know what to say about this book. Genuinely, I don't. So in place of a review I'm going to describe my experience of it.<br/>It has the most heart felt beginning I have ever read, yet the more I read it the more I realised how many rules it broke as a novel. There is a tremendous amount of telling in it, the author directly talks to you and is himself in it as a character, he even has real and famous people characterised in certain aspects, just to prove a point. Yet, throughout all</span>
  <span id="freeText7449297209144917922" style="display:none">I genuinely don't know what to say about this book. Genuinely, I don't. So in place of a review I'm going to describe my experience of it.<br />It has the most heart felt beginning I have ever read, yet the more I read it the more I realised how many rules it broke as a novel. There is a tremendous amount of telling in it, the author directly talks to you and is himself in it as a character, he even has real and famous people characterised in certain aspects, just to prove a point. Yet, throughout all of that I couldn't help but love it. I'll give you an example:<br />There is a part in the book completely irrelevant to the rest of the story. It takes up a good portion of the end of the novel, it has no place anywhere in it and yet, it simply belonged exactly where it was, which is, the wrong place. Does that make it the right place? I guess so, though I am not sure.<br />This book is brilliant. You don't read it, you have it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7449297209144917922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1557485551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1557485551" />
    <a title="Christos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1950744-christos"><img alt="Christos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366334287p2/1950744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1557485551?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christos" href="/user/show/1950744-christos">Christos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060932381" href="/book/show/397256.Immortality">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1557485551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6152669729597756430">This was an out and out struggle to finish, Part Four: Homo Sentimentalis was essentially unreadable gibberish. There's some good thoughts and writing in here, but the self indulgent, random mashup of characters and famous folk past and present, as well as the scattered author appearances are distracting. Ultimately I was left feeling that this book deserves no immortality and should be mercifully euthanized for the benefit of good books (and patient readers) everywhere. 2.5 stars rounded down.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bVtp3gGwAII3CDzd5EwjV1eelzBN/78vtpnzAvlDDaahWM+/8sq4y2qEQK5LAX2VmiKVCD9xO0zF+UrOxMDSag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cASADQKXqiSO32zv9Dns1tIMsAaOWwrUfqH6BLzS9ny8ByZs8e0SbdNTEJxbdLIUH7CyPvzVjrcNwUPIgVEpsA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3224911412807430911">Milan Kundera is a Czech and French writer of Czech origin who has lived in exile in France since 1975, where he became a naturalized French citizen in 1981. He is best known for <i>The Unbearable Lightness of Being</i>, <i>The Book of Laughter and Forgetting</i>, and <i>The Joke</i>.<br/><br/>Kundera has written in both Czech and French. He revises the French translations of all his books; these therefore are not considered tr</span>
  <span id="freeText3224911412807430911" style="display:none">Milan Kundera is a Czech and French writer of Czech origin who has lived in exile in France since 1975, where he became a naturalized French citizen in 1981. He is best known for <i>The Unbearable Lightness of Being</i>, <i>The Book of Laughter and Forgetting</i>, and <i>The Joke</i>.<br /><br />Kundera has written in both Czech and French. He revises the French translations of all his books; these therefore are not considered translations but original works. <br /><br />Due to censorship by the Communist government of Czechoslovakia, his books were banned from his native country, and that remained the case until the downfall of this government in the Velvet Revolution of 1989. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3224911412807430911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2776625-nesmrtelnost">Quotes from Immortality</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;<i>I think, therefore I am</i> is the statement of an intellectual who underrates toothaches. <i>I feel, therefore I am</i> is a truth much more universally valid, and it applies to everything that's alive. My self does not differ substantially from yours in terms of its thought. Many people, few ideas: we all think more or less the same, and we exchange, borrow, steal thoughts from one another. However, when someone steps on my foot, only I feel the pain. The basis of the self is not thought but suffering, which is the most fundamental of all feelings. While it suffers, not even a cat can doubt its unique and uninterchangeable self. In intense suffering the world disappears and each of us is alone with his self. Suffering is the university of egocentrism.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/291124-i-think-therefore-i-am-is-the-statement-of-an">269 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Just imagine living in a world without mirrors. You'd dream about your face and imagine it as an outer reflection of what is inside you. And then, when you reached forty, someone put a mirror before you for the first time in your life. Imagine your fright! You'd see the face of a stranger. And you'd know quite clearly what you are unable to grasp: your face is not you.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/367028-just-imagine-living-in-a-world-without-mirrors-you-d-dream">231 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/2776625-nesmrtelnost">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
